==Latin==

===Etymology===
From {{affix|la|aborior|-scō}}.

===Verb===
{{la-verb|aborīscor|aborīscī|conj=3|pattern=depon-noperf}}

# I [[perish]], [[die]].

====Inflection====
{{la-conj-3rd|type=depon-noperf|aborīsc}}

====Synonyms====
* {{sense|perish, die}} {{l|la|aborior}}

====Antonyms====
* {{sense|perish, die}} {{l|la|nāscor}}, {{l|la|spīrō}}

==Latin==

===Etymology===
From {{affix|la|ad-|gloss1=near, at; towards, to|discō|gloss2=learn; study}}.

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|addiscō}}

===Verb===
{{la-verb|addiscō|addiscere|addidicī|conj=3|pattern=nopass}}

# I [[learn]] [[in addition]] to or [[further]].
# I am [[informed]], [[hear]], learn.

====Inflection====
{{la-conj-3rd|type=nopass|addisc|addidic}}

====Related terms====

* {{l|la|condisco|condiscō}}
* {{l|la|dedisco|dēdiscō}}

* {{l|la|edisco|ēdiscō}}

==Latin==

===Alternative forms===
* {{l|la|adormīscō}}

===Etymology===
From {{affix|la|ad-|gloss1=to, towards, at|dormīscō|gloss2=fall asleep}}.

===Verb===
{{la-verb|addormīscō|addormīscere|conj=3|pattern=nopass-noperf}}

# I [[fall asleep]], [[go to sleep]].

====Inflection====
* This verb is [[defective verb|defective]], with only those forms based on the first principal part.
{{la-conj-3rd|type=nopass-noperf|addormīsc}}

====Synonyms====
* {{sense|fall asleep}} {{l|la|dormisco|dormīscō}}

====Related terms====
* {{l|la|addormio|addormiō}}
* {{l|la|dormio|dormiō}}
* {{l|la|dormisco|dormīscō}}

====Descendants====
* Galician: {{l|ga|adormecer}}
* Old Portuguese: {{l|roa-opt|adormecer}}
* Portuguese: {{l|pt|adormecer}}
* Spanish: {{l|es|adormecer}}

===References===

* {{R:Gaffiot}}

Page 236 adipiscor: Found match for regex: =
Page 236 adipiscor: -------- begin text ---------
==Latin==

===Etymology===
From {{affix|la|ad-|gloss1=to, towards, at|apīscor|gloss2=reach after something, pursue; reach}}.

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|adipīscor}}

===Verb===
{{la-verb|adipīscor|adipīscī|adeptus sum|conj=3|pattern=depon}}

# I [[arrive]] at, [[reach]]; [[overtake]], [[catch]] up with.
# I [[get]], [[obtain]], [[acquire]], get [[possession]] of, [[achieve]].

====Usage notes====
Since this verb is deponent, its past participle {{m|la|adeptus}} usually has an '''active''' sense ("having obtained"). But along with a few other (e.g. {{m|la|comitatus}} from {{m|la|comitor}}, {{m|la|complexus}} from {{m|la|complector}}) it can sometimes have a '''passive''' sense too ("obtained"), as in ''adepta libertate'' found in Sallustius.

====Inflection====
{{la-conj-3rd|type=depon|adipīsc|adept}}

====Synonyms====
* {{sense|obtain}} {{l|la|consequor|cōnsequor}}, {{l|la|exoro|exōrō}}, {{l|la|impetro|impetrō}}, {{l|la|mereo|mereō}}.

====Usage notes====
* {{m|la||adipiscing}} (not a real Latin word) is a {{m|en|lorem ipsum}}.

===References===
* {{R:L&S}}
* {{R:Elementary Lewis}}
* {{R:Gaffiot}}
* {{R:M&A}}
-------- end text --------

==Latin==

===Etymology===
From {{affix|la|apiō|-scō|pos1=alternative form of {{m|la|apō||I fasten}}}}. Cognate with {{cog|grc|ἅπτω||I fasten, grasp, enkindle}}, {{cog|sa|आप्त||to reach, gain, take possession of}}, {{m|sa|आप्नोति||to obtain, to grasp}}, {{cog|hit|𒂊𒅁||to take, seize, grab|tr=epp-}}<ref>{{R:hit:Kloekhorst}}</ref>.

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|apīscor}}

===Verb===
{{la-verb|apīscor|apīscī|aptus sum|conj=3|pattern=depon}}

# I [[reach]] after, try to [[seize]]
# I [[pursue]]
# I [[attain]] or [[acquire]]

====Inflection====
{{la-conj-3rd|type=depon|apīsc|apt}}

====Derived terms====
* {{l|la|adipīscor}}
* {{l|la|indipīscor}}
* {{l|la|redipīscor}}

===References===
<references />

===Further reading===
* {{R:L&S}}
* {{R:Elementary Lewis}}
* {{R:Gaffiot}}
* {{R:Century 1911|apt}}
* {{R:Sihler 1995}}

==Latin==

===Alternative forms===
* {{l|la|adscīscō}}

===Etymology===
From {{affix|la|ad-|scīscō|gloss2=seek to know; learn; approve}}.

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|ascīscō}}

===Verb===
{{la-verb|ascīscō|ascīscere|ascīvī|ascītum|conj=3}}

# I [[take]] or [[receive]] something with [[knowledge]]; [[approve]], [[accept]], [[recognize]], [[adopt]].
# I take or receive someone to myself; [[bring in]], [[win over]], [[recruit]], adopt, [[associate]] with myself.
# {{lb|la|with reflexive or dative}} I [[assume]], [[claim]] or [[arrogate]] something to myself, [[lay claim]] to.

====Inflection====
{{la-conj-3rd|ascīsc|ascīv|ascīt}}

====Synonyms====
* {{sense|arrogate something to myself}} {{l|la|arrogō}}

====Related terms====
{{top2}}
* {{l|la|cōnscīscō}}
* {{l|la|dēscīscō}}
* {{l|la|perscīscō}}
{{mid2}}
* {{l|la|rescīscō}}
* {{l|la|scīscō}}
{{bottom}}

===References===
* {{R:L&S}}
* {{R:Elementary Lewis}}
* {{R:Gaffiot}}
* {{R:M&A}}

{{also|Disco|discó}}
==English==

===Etymology===
From a shortening of {{m|en|discotheque}}, from {{etyl|fr|en}} {{m|fr|discothèque}}.

===Pronunciation===
* {{a|UK}} {{IPA|/ˈdɪskəʊ/|lang=en}}
* {{a|US}} {{IPA|/ˈdɪskoʊ/|lang=en}}
* {{rhymes|ɪskəʊ|lang=en}}
* {{hyphenation|dis|co|lang=en}}

===Noun===
{{en-noun|~}}

# {{lb|en|countable|slightly|dated}} {{clipping of|lang=en|discotheque}}, a [[nightclub]] for [[dancing]].
# {{lb|en|uncountable}} A [[genre]] of [[dance]] [[music]] that was popular in the [[1970s]], characterized by elements of [[soul music]] with a strong Latin-American beat and often accompanied by pulsating lights.

====Synonyms====
* {{sense|place for dancing}} [[club]], [[nightclub]]

==Latin==

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|discō|eccl=1}}

===Etymology 1===
{{PIE root|la|deḱ}}
From {{inh|la|itc-pro|*dikskō}}, reduplicated form of {{der|la|ine-pro|*deḱ-}}. From the same root as {{m|la|doceō}}; unrelated to {{m|la|discipulus}}.

Cognates include Ancient Greek {{m|grc|διδάσκω}}, {{m|grc|δεδαώς}}, {{m|grc|δαῆναι}}, {{m|grc|δέχομαι}}.

====Verb====
{{la-verb|discō|discere|didicī|discitum|conj=3}}

# I [[learn]]
#: ''Aut '''disce''' aut discede.''
#:: Either '''learn''' or go away.
# {{lb|la|drama}} I [[study]], [[practice]]

=====Inflection=====
{{la-conj-3rd|disc|didic|discit}}

=====Derived terms=====
* {{l|la|dēdiscō}}
* {{l|la|ēdiscō}}

=====Descendants=====
* Welsh: {{l|cy|dysgu}}

===Etymology 2===
{{nonlemma}}

====Noun====
{{la-noun-form|discō}}

# {{inflection of|discus||dat|s|lang=la}}
# {{inflection of|discus||abl|s|lang=la}}

==Latin==

===Alternative forms===
* {{l|la|glīscor}}

===Etymology===
Of uncertain origin<ref>{{R:la:WH|head=glisco|page=607|vol=1}}</ref>; proposed derivations include:
* From {{der|la|ine-pro|*ǵʰelh₃-||to shine}}. Cognate with {{cog|la|gilvus}}, {{m|la|helvus}} and {{cog|grc|χλιάω||to be warm}}.
* From {{der|la|ine-pro|*gel-||form into a ball; ball}}. Cognates include {{cog|la|glaeba}}, {{m|la|glomus}} and {{cog|en|clump}}.

===Verb===
{{la-verb|glīscō|glīscere|conj=3|pattern=nopass-noperf}}

# I [[swell]], [[spread]], [[blaze]] up, [[increase]]

====Inflection====
{{la-conj-3rd|type=nopass-noperf|glīsc}}

===References===
* {{R:L&S}}
* {{R:Elementary Lewis}}
* {{R:Gaffiot}}
<references/>

===Etymology===
From {{affix|la|hiō|t1=to yawn, gape|-scō}}.

* {{la-IPA|hīscō}}

# {{lb|la|intransitive}} I open the mouth, [[mutter]], [[murmur]].
# {{lb|la|transitive}} I [[speak]], [[utter]].

====Inflection====
* This verb is [[defective verb|defective]], with only those forms based on the first principal part.
{{la-conj-3rd|type=noperf|hīsc}}

==Latin==

===Etymology===
From {{prefix|la|in|id1=in|nōscō|alt2=(g)nōscō}}.

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|ignōscō}}

===Verb===
{{la-verb|ignōscō|ignōscere|ignōvī|ignōtum|conj=3}}

# I [[forgive]].

====Usage notes====
Takes the dative form of the person forgiven.

====Inflection====
Passive forms are not known except for the third-person singular.
{{la-conj-3rd|ignōsc|ignōv|ignōt}}

====Descendants====
* Italian: {{l|it|ignoscere}} (archaic)
* Spanish: {{l|es|iñocer}} (archaic)
===References===
* {{R:L&S}}
* {{R:Elementary Lewis}}
* {{R:Gaffiot}}

==Latin==

===Etymology===
{{back-formation|la|īrātus}}, as though it were the participle of a first-conjugation verb, with inchoative {{affix|la|-scō}} added.<ref>{{R:De Vaan 2008}}</ref>

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|īrāscor}}

===Verb===
{{la-verb|īrāscor|īrāscī|īrātus sum|conj=3|pattern=depon}}

# I am [[angry]], I am [[enraged]]

====Inflection====
{{la-conj-3rd|type=depon|īrāsc|īrāt}}

==Latin==

===Etymology===
{{PIE root|la|h₂neḱ|id=think}}
From {{inh|la|ine-pro|*h₂eh₂nóḱe||has reached, attained}}, perfective of {{m|ine-pro|*h₂neḱ-||to reach}}. Cognate with {{cog|sga|doánaic|(do·)ánaic|came, arrived}}, {{cog|sq|kënaq||to satisfy, be enough}}, {{cog|lt|nèšti||to carry}}, {{cog|grc|ἤνεγκα||I carried}} (aorist of {{m|grc|φέρω}}), {{cog|ang|ġenōg||enough}}, {{cog|cu|нести||to carry}}, {{cog|sa|अश्नोति|tr=aśnóti}}, {{m|sa|नशति|tr=náśati||attains}}.

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|nancīscor}}

===Verb===
{{la-verb|nancīscor|nancīscī|nactus sum|conj=3|pattern=depon}}

# I [[meet with]], [[stumble]] on, [[encounter]], [[acquire]], [[get]], [[reach]], [[find]] something.
#: {{uxi|la|cum plus otii nactus ero|t=when I have more free time (lit. ''when I will have met more leisure'')}}
# I [[contract]], [[catch]].
#: {{uxi|la|morbum nancisci|t=to fall ill}}
# {{lb|la|by extension}} I [[possess]] by [[birth]], have by [[nature]].

====Inflection====
* The fourth principal part may be {{m|la|nactus}} or {{m|la|nānctus}} sum.
{{la-conj-3rd|type=depon|nancīsc|nact}}

====Synonyms====
* {{sense|obtain}} {{l|la|adipīscor}}, {{l|la|cōnsequor}}, {{l|la|exōrō}}, {{l|la|impetrō}}, {{l|la|mereō}}

====Derived terms====
* {{l|la|nanciō}}

===References===
* {{R:L&S}}
* {{R:Elementary Lewis}}
* {{R:Gaffiot}}
* {{R:M&A}}

==Latin==

===Etymology===
{{PIE root|la|ǵenh₁}}
From earlier {{m|la|gnāscor}}, from {{der|la|itc-pro|*gnāskōr}}, from {{der|la|ine-pro|*ǵenh₁-}}. Cognate with Ancient Greek {{m|grc|γεννάω||to beget}}.

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|nāscor}}

===Verb===
{{la-verb|nāscor|nāscī|nātus sum|conj=3|pattern=depon}}

# I am [[born]], begotten
# I [[arise]], [[proceed]]
# I [[grow]], spring forth
# I [[am]] a number of years old
#: ''Viginti et quinque annos natus sum.''
#:: I am 25 years old.
#* [[w:Terence|Terence]], ''Heauton Timuromenos'' 62-63
#*: ''Annos sexaginta natus es...''
#*:: You are 60 years old...

====Inflection====
* Note: Future participle is sometimes {{m|la|nāscitūrus}}.
{{la-conj-3rd|type=depon|nāsc|nāt}}

====Related terms====
* {{l|la|nāscēns}}
* {{l|la|nāscō}} / {{l|la|nāscere}}
* {{l|la|nātālīcius}}
* {{l|la|nātālis}}
* {{l|la|nātiō}}
* {{l|la|nātīvus}}
* {{l|la|nātūra}}

==Italian==

===Etymology===
From {{der|it|LL.|noscum}}, from {{der|it|la|nōbiscum||with us}}.

===Pronunciation===
* {{IPA|/ˈnɔs.ko/|[ˈn̺ɔs̪ko]|lang=it}}
* {{rhymes|ɔsko|lang=it}}
* {{it-stress|nòsco}}
* {{hyph|no|sco|lang=it}}

===Pronoun===
{{head|it|pronoun}} {{tcx|poetic|archaic|lang=it}}

# [[with]] [[us]]
#* {{quote-book|author=Dante Alighieri|authorlink=Dante Alighieri|title=[[w:Purgatorio|La divina commedia: Purgatorio]]|trans-title=The Divine Comedy: Purgatory|format=paperback|lang=it|publisher=Bompiani|year=1321|year_published=2001|page=340|section=Canto XXII|lines=106–108|passage=Euripide v'è '''nosco''' e Antifonte, ¶ Simonide, Agatone e altri piùe ¶ Greci che già di lauro ornar la fronte.|translation=Euripides is '''with us''', Antiphon, ¶ Simonides, Agatho, and many other ¶ Greeks who of old their brows with laurel decked.}}
#* {{quote-book|lang=it|author=[[w:Vincenzo Monti|Vincenzo Monti]], transl.|title=[[w:Iliad|Iliade]]|trans-title=Iliad|url=https://books.google.it/books?id=oJkHAAAAQAAJ&lpg=PA324&hl=it&pg=PA3#v=onepage&q&f=false|location=Milan|publisher=Giovanni Resnati e Gius. Bernardoni di Gio|chapter=Libro IV|trans-chapter=Book 4|year=1825|year_published=1840|page=85|pageurl=https://books.google.it/books?id=oJkHAAAAQAAJ&lpg=PA324&hl=it&pg=PA85#v=onepage&q&f=false|original=Ἰλιάς (''Iliás'')|by={{w|Homer}}|passage={{...}} chi primiero ¶ L'accordo vïolò, pasto vedrassi ¶ Di voraci avoltoi, mentre captive ¶ Le dilette lor mogli in un co' figli ¶ Noi '''nosco''' condurremo, Ilio distrutto.|translation=those who first broke the agreeement will be meal for hungry vultures, while we take '''with us''' their beloved wives and children, after destroying Troy.}}
# {{lb|it|by extension}} [[among]] us
# {{lb|it|by extension}} [[towards]] or [[against]] us
# {{lb|it|by extension}} in our [[time]]

==Latin==

===Alternative forms===
* {{l|la|gnōscō}}

===Etymology===
{{PIE root|la|ǵneh₃}}
From earlier {{m|la|gnōscō}}, from {{inh|la|itc-pro|*gnōskō}}, from {{inh|la|ine-pro|*ǵn̥h₃sḱéti}}.

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|eccl=yes|nōscō}}

===Verb===
{{la-verb|nōscō|nōscere|nōvī|nōtum|conj=3}}

# I [[know]], [[recognize]], am acquainted with, i.e.; in possession of knowledge.
#* ''Hic Natus Ubique '''Notus'''''
#*: Born Here, '''Known''' Everywhere ([[motto]] of the [https://web.archive.org/web/20051120113742/http://www.instituto-allende.edu.mx/english/misc/ANESA.htm Allende Institute] in reference to [[w:Ignacio Allende|Ignacio de Allende]])

====Inflection====
* Also in classical Latin are ''nōram'' for ''nōveram'', ''nōrim'' for ''nōverim'', ''nōmus'' for ''nōvimus'', ''nōrunt'' for ''nōvērunt''.
{{la-conj-3rd|nōsc|nōv|nōt|sync_perf=poet}}

Page 3461 obliviscor: -------- begin text ---------
==Latin==

===Etymology===
Uncertain. Probably from {{affix|la|ob-}} plus a derivative of {{m|la|lēvis||smooth}} with ''-ēscor'' (passive inchoative suffix, from [[-esco|-ēscō]]), with ''oblīvīscor'' having an earlier meaning of "I start to erase".

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|oblīvīscor}}

===Verb===
{{la-verb|oblīvīscor|oblīvīscī|oblītus sum|conj=3|pattern=depon}}

# I [[lose]] [[remembrance]] of, [[forget]] (+gen. of person or gen/acc. of person or thing).
# I forget, [[disregard]], [[omit]], [[neglect]] (+gen. of person or gen/acc. of person or thing).

====Usage notes====
Usually used with the genitive.

====Inflection====
{{la-conj-3rd|type=depon|oblīvīsc|oblīt}}

====Derived terms====
* {{l|la|oblitus|oblītus}}
* {{l|la|oblivio|oblīviō}}
* {{l|la|oblivium|oblīvium}}

====Related terms====
* {{l|la|oblivialis|oblīviālis}}
* {{l|la|obliviosus|oblīviōsus}}
* {{l|la|oblivius|oblīvius}}

====Descendants====
{{top2}}
* Aromanian: {{l|rup|ultu}}, {{l|rup|ultari}}
* Asturian: {{l|ast|olvidar}}
* Catalan: {{l|ca|oblidar}}
* English: {{l|en|obliviate}}, {{l|en|oblivion}}
* Franco-Provençal: {{l|frp|oubliar}}
* French: {{l|fr|oublier}}
{{mid2}}
* Italian: {{l|it|obliare}}, {{l|it|obbliare}}
* Occitan: {{l|oc|doblidar}}
* Portuguese: {{l|pt|olvidar}}
* Romanian: {{l|ro|uita}}, {{l|ro|uitare}}
* Romansh: {{l|rm|emblidar}}, {{l|rm|amblidar}}, {{l|rm|invlidar}}
* Sardinian: {{l|sc|olvidai}}, {{l|sc|olvidare}}, {{l|sc|orbidare}}, {{l|sc|ulvidare}}
* Spanish: {{l|es|olvidar}}
{{bottom}}

===References===
* {{R:L&S}}
* {{R:Elementary Lewis}}
* {{R:Gaffiot}}
-------- end text --------

==Latin==

===Etymology===
From {{affix|la|pacō|gloss1=to come to an agreement|-scō|gloss2=inchoative suffix}}, from {{der|la|ine-pro|*peh₂ḱ-||agreement, peace}}, also the source of {{cog|la|pāx||peace}} and {{cog|la|pactum||agreement, means}}.

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|eccl=yes|pacīscor}}

===Verb===
{{la-verb|pacīscor|pacīscī|pactus sum|conj=3|pattern=depon}}

# I make a [[bargain]], [[contract]] or [[agreement]] with

====Inflection====
{{la-conj-3rd|type=depon|pācisc|pāct}}

====Derived terms====
* {{l|la|pactum}}

====Related terms====
* {{l|la|pacō}}
* {{l|la|compecīscor}}
* {{l|la|compectum}}
* {{l|la|pāx}}
* {{l|la|pācō}}

===References===
* {{R:L&S}}
* {{R:Elementary Lewis}}
* {{R:Gaffiot}}
* {{R:De Vaan 2008|452|pāx}}

==Italian==

===Noun===
{{it-noun|m}} (''Variant of'': [[pascolo]])

# [[pasture]]
# [[feeding]]
# [[food]]

===Verb===
{{head|it|verb form}}

# {{inflection of|pascere||1|s|pres|indc|lang=it}}

===Anagrams===
* [[scapo#Italian|scapo]], [[scopa#Italian|scopa]]

----

==Latin==

===Etymology===
{{PIE root|la|peh₂}}
From {{inh|la|itc-pro|*pāskō}}, from {{inh|la|ine-pro|*peh₂-||to protect}}.

Cognates include Ancient Greek {{m|grc|ποιμήν||shepherd}}, Sanskrit {{m|sa|पाति|tr=pā́ti||to protect}}, Old English {{m|ang|fōda}} and {{m|ang|fedan|fēdan}} (English {{m|en|food}} and {{m|en|feed}}), Old Church Slavonic {{m|cu|пасти|tr=pasti||to pasture}}, {{bor|ru|cu|пища}}.

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|pāscō}}

===Verb===
{{la-verb|pāscō|pāscere|pāvī|pāstum|conj=3}}

# I [[feed]], [[nourish]], maintain, support.
# I [[pasture]], drive to pasture, attend.
# I feed, [[supply]], [[cultivate]], let grow
# {{lb|la|of animals}} I [[graze]], browse
# {{lb|la|figuratively}} I feast, delight, satisfy, feed, gratify
# I consume, lay waste, ravage, desolate

====Inflection====
{{la-conj-3rd|pāsc|pāv|pāst|sync_perf=poet}}

====Derived terms====
* {{l|la|pāstus}}
* {{l|la|dēpāscō}}

====Related terms====
* {{l|la|pāscitō}}
* {{l|la|pāscuus}}
* {{l|la|pāstor}}

====Descendants====
{{top2}}
* Aromanian: {{l|rup|pascu}}, {{l|rup|pashtiri}}
* Asturian: {{l|ast|pacer}}
* Catalan: {{l|ca|péixer}}
* Corsican: {{l|co|pascia}}
* Dalmatian: {{l|dlm|puoscro}}
* English: {{l|en|pasture}}, {{l|en|repast}}
* French: {{l|fr|paître}}
* Friulian: {{l|fur|passi}}, {{l|fur|paši}}
* Galician: {{l|gl|pacer}}
{{mid2}}
* Italian: {{l|it|pascere}}
* Occitan: {{l|oc|pàisser}}, {{l|oc|pàsquer}}
* Portuguese: {{l|pt|pascer}}
* Romanian: {{l|ro|paște}}, {{l|ro|paștere}}
* Sicilian: {{l|scn|pàsciri}}
* Sardinian: {{l|sc|paschere}}, {{l|sc|paschi}}, {{l|sc|pasci}}, {{l|sc|pasciri}}, {{l|sc|passere}}

* Venetian: {{l|vec|pàser}}, {{l|vec|pàsar}}

Page 3908 posco: -------- begin text ---------
==Latin==

===Etymology===
{{PIE root|la|preḱ}}
From {{inh|la|itc-pro|*porskō}}, from {{inh|la|ine-pro|*pr̥sḱéti}}, from {{m|ine-pro|*preḱ-||to ask, ask for}} + {{m|ine-pro|*-sḱéti||imperfective suffix}}. {{cog|la|-esco||pos=inchoative suffix}} derives separately from this ending.

Cognates include {{cog|la|prex||prayer}}, {{cog|la|procus||suitor}}, Sanskrit {{m|sa|पृच्छति|tr=pṛccháti}}, Old Armenian {{m|xcl|հարց|}}, Old Church Slavonic {{m|cu|sc=Cyrs|просити|tr=prositi}}, and Old English {{m|ang|friġnan}} (English {{m|en|frain}}).

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|poscō}}
* {{la-IPA|pōscō}}, [ˈpos.koː]

===Verb===
{{la-verb|poscō|head2=pōscō|poscere|inf2=pōscere|poposcī|perf2=popōscī|conj=3|pattern=nopass}}

# I [[beg]], I [[demand]], I [[request]], I [[desire]].
#: {{ux|la|'''Poscor''' aliquid.|t=Something is '''asked''' of me.|inline=1}}
#: {{ux|la|'''Poscor''' meum Laelapa.|t=They '''demand''' of me my Laelaps.|inline=1}}
# I [[demand]] for [[punishment]], I ask the [[surrender]] of.
# I [[call]] someone.
#* {{Q|la|Plautus|Curculio|5|3|5|quote=''Argentariis male credi qui aiunt, nugas praedicant: nam et bene et male credi dico; id adeo ego hodie expertus sum. Non male creditur qui numquam reddunt, sed prorsum perit. Vel ille, decem minas dum solvit, omnis mensas transiit. Postquam nil fit, clamore hominem '''posco''': ille in ius me vocat; pessume metui, ne mihi hodie apud praetorem solveret. Verum amici compulerunt: reddit argentum domo. Nunc domum properare certumst.''<ref>[http://www.thelatinlibrary.com/plautus/curculio.shtml Latin]</ref>|trans=People that say bankers are ill trusted talk rubbish. Why, they are well and ill trusted both, I tell you–and what is more, I have proved it myself this very day. Money is not ill trusted to men that never repay you; it is gone for good. That Lyco, for example, in trying to raise forty pounds for me, went to every single bank. Nothing coming of it, I begin '''dunning''' him at the top of my lungs. He summons me before the magistrate I was horribly afraid he would settle with me in court. But his friends coerced him, and he paid me out of his own cash in hand. Now I must hurry home.<ref>[http://artemis.austincollege.edu/acad/cml/rcape/comedy/5-3.html English]</ref>}}
#: {{ux|la|Ego '''poscor''' Olympo!|t=It is I that Olympus '''summons'''!|inline=1}}
#: {{ux|la|Ad te confugio et supplex tua numina '''posco'''.|t=To you I have recourse and, as a suppliant, I '''call''' on your divine power.|inline=1}}
# I [[ask]] in [[marriage]], I demand one's hand.
#: {{ux|la|Filiam tuam mihi uxorem '''posco'''.|t=I '''demand''' your daughter's hand in marriage.|inline=1}}

====Usage notes====
Though it is listed without passive forms, they do sometimes appear, as in Seneca's Thyestes, 242-43: "Tantalum et Pelopem aspice; / ad haec manus exempla '''poscuntur''' meae."

====Inflection====
With short o:
{{la-conj-3rd|type=no-pasv-perf|posc|poposc}}
With long o:
{{la-conj-3rd|type=no-pasv-perf|pōsc|pōposc}}

====Synonyms====
* {{sense|beg, demand}} {{l|la|flāgitō}}, {{l|la|postulō}}, {{l|la|petō}}

====Derived terms====
* {{l|la|postulō}}

====References====
* {{R:L&S}}
* {{R:Elementary Lewis}}
* {{R:Gaffiot}}
* {{R:M&A}}

====Usage notes====
* Often in constructions using {{m|la|dē}}, the accusative and infinitive or an indirect question.

==Latin==

===Etymology===
From {{suffix|la|sciō|scō||gloss1=know}}.

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|scīscō|eccl=yes}}

===Verb===
{{la-verb|scīscō|scīscere|scīvī|scītum|conj=3}}

# {{lb|la|transitive}} I [[seek]] to [[know]]; [[ask]], [[search]], [[inquire]], [[question]].
# {{lb|la|transitive}} I [[accept]], [[approve]], [[assent]] to, [[vote]] for; [[appoint]], [[enact]], [[decree]], [[ordain]].
# {{lb|la|transitive}} I [[learn]], [[ascertain]], [[know]].

====Inflection====
{{la-conj-3rd|scīsc|scīv|scīt}}

====Derived terms====
{{top2}}
* {{l|la|ascīscō}}
* {{l|la|cōnscīscō}}
* {{l|la|dēscīscō}}
* {{l|la|perscīscō}}
* {{l|la|rescīscō}}
{{mid2}}
* {{l|la|scīscitor}}
* {{l|la|scītor}}
* {{l|la|scītum}}
* {{l|la|scītus}}
{{bottom}}

====Related terms====
{{top2}}
* {{l|la|sciō}}
* {{l|la|scītāmenta}}
* {{l|la|scītātiō}}

* {{l|la|scītē}}
* {{l|la|scītulus}}

==Latin==

===Alternative forms===
* {{l|la|ulcīscō}} {{i|archaic}}

===Etymology===
From {{der|la|ine-pro|*h₂elk-||}}. Cognate with Ancient Greek {{m|grc|ἀλκή}}<ref>{{cite-book
|title=Etymological Dictionary of Greek
|first=Robert S. P.
|last=Beekes
|publisher=Brill Academic Publishers
|location=Leiden
|year=2009
|isbn=9789004174184
|page=70
}}</ref>. Confer with {{m|la|arceō}}.

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|ulcīscor}}

===Verb===
{{la-verb|ulcīscor|ulcīscī|ultus sum|conj=3|pattern=depon}}

# I [[avenge]].
# I take [[vengeance]] on.

====Inflection====
{{la-conj-3rd|type=depon|ulcīsc|ult}}

====Synonyms====
* {{sense|avenge}} {{l|la|punio|pūniō}}, {{l|la|vindico|vindicō}}
* {{sense|take vengeance on}} {{l|la|persequor}}, {{l|la|punio|pūniō}}, {{l|la|vindico|vindicō}}

====Related terms====
* {{l|la|inultus}}
* {{l|la|ultio|ultiō}}
* {{l|la|ultor}}
* {{l|la|ultorius|ultōrius}}
* {{l|la|ultrix|ultrīx}}

==Latin==

===Etymology===
From {{m|la|vespera||evening}}

===Pronunciation===
* {{la-IPA|vesperāscō}}

===Verb===
{{la-verb|vesperāscō|vesperāscere|vesperāvī|conj=3|pattern=nopass}}

# grow towards [[evening]]; become evening

====Usage notes====
* The [[supine]] stem is unattested.

====Inflection====
{{la-conj-3rd|type=nopass|vesperāsc|vesperāv}}

====Derived terms====
* {{l|la|advesperāscit}}

====Related terms====
* {{l|la|vesper}}
* {{l|la|vespera}}

===References===
* {{R:L&S}}
* {{R:Elementary Lewis}}
* {{R:Gaffiot}}

[[Category:la:Time]]

==Latin==

===Etymology===
From {{affix|la|veterō|-scō}}.

===Verb===
{{la-verb|veterāscō|veterāscere|conj=3|pattern=nopass-noperf}}

# I [[wear out]]

{{la-conj-3rd|type=nopass-noperf|veterāsc}}
